Given the fact that Google has become so good at crawling fresh content, the date of first-crawl is often the same as the actual publication date (#1).</p> \n<p>#3. <strong>The cache date</strong> - this is the date when a web page was last crawled by the Googlebot. Search engines&nbsp;often&nbsp;re-crawl web pages every few days or weeks, sometimes multiple times in a day in the case of news websites, to check if the content has been updated or changed.</p> \n<h2 id=\"find-the-publishing-date-of-web-pages\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/search/find-publishing-date-of-web-pages/8410/#find-the-publishing-date-of-web-pages\" aria-label=\"find the publishing date of web pages permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Find&nbsp;the Publishing Date of Web Pages</h2> \n<p>Most <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/old-newspaper-articles/18689/\">news articles</a> include the original publishing date in the article itself. However, in situations where the publishing date is not available, or if you think that the printed date is incorrect, you can use a simple Google trick to know when that web page was last published on the Internet.</p> \n<p><img src=\"https://www.labnol.org/images/2008/web-page-publish-date.png\" alt=\"Web Page Publishing Date\" title=\"Web Page Publishing Date\" /> Google can tell the date when a web page was first published on the Web.</p> \n<p><strong>Step 1.</strong> Go to google.com and copy-paste the full URL of any&nbsp;web page in the search box &nbsp;and prefix it with the <code class=\"language-text\">inurl:</code> operator.</p> \n<p>For instance, if the URL of the page is page is:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">https://www.example.com</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>You should write the URL in the Google Search box as:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">inurl:https://www.example.com</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>Press the Search button and the URL in your browser address bar would read something like this:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">https://www.google.com/search?q=inurl:https://www.example.com</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p><strong>Step 2.</strong> Now go your browser’s address bar - press Ctrl+L on a Windows machine or Cmd+L on Mac - and append <code class=\"language-text\">&amp;as_qdr=y25</code> to the end of the Google search URL. Press enter again.</p> \n<p>The modified Google search URL would become:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">https://www.google.com/search?q=inurl:https://www.example.com&amp;as_qdr=y25</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>The <code class=\"language-text\">as_qdr=y25</code> parameter instructs Google to do a date-based search and retrieve pages that have been indexed by the Googlebot in the past 25 years (in other words, everything).</p> \n<p>Also see: <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/gmail-search-tips/29206/\">Search Emails by Date in Gmail</a></p> \n<p><strong>Step 3.</strong> Google will load the search results again but this time, you’ll see the actual publication date of the web page next to the title in Google search results as in the above screenshot.</p> \n<p>This trick should help if you <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/cite-tweets-apa-mla-style/20985/\">citing tweets</a> (MLA or APA style) or <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/tech/cite-web-pages-mla-style/13548/\">citing web pages</a> (MLA style) in your papers.</p> \n<h2 id=\"how-old-is-a-web-page\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/search/find-publishing-date-of-web-pages/8410/#how-old-is-a-web-page\" aria-label=\"how old is a web page permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>How old is a web page</h2> \n<p>Because Google can crawl any page the moment it is published on the Internet, the indexed date appearing in search results is often accurate.</p> \n<p>However, if the content of a web page was updated after the first Google crawl, the publishing date may indicate the date when it was most recently edited by the website and not the date when it was first indexed or published on the Internet.</p> \n<p><iframe width=\"100%\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/8av33eceD08?rel=0\" frameBorder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p> \n<p>Also see: <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/tools/best-online-tools-for-webmasters-know-everything-about-websites/2744/\">Know everything about a website</a></p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Tue, 28 Apr 2020 17:00:28 00:45:54","updatedTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","title":"How to Create a Disposable Email Address with Gmail","link":"https://www.labnol.org/internet/disposable-email-address/28072/","description":"<p>A temporary email address is very useful when you don’t want to share your real email address with a website. There are a plethora of services - <a href=\"https://10minutemail.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">10 Minute Email</a>, <a href=\"https://www.mailinator.com/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Mailinator</a> and <a href=\"https://maildrop.cc/\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">MailDrop</a> to name a few - that will mask your main email address behind a temporary alias and thus save your inbox from potential spam.</p> \n<p>The only problem with using disposable email addresses is that it requires some work. You first need to generate a temporary address, paste it into the web form and then manually check the disposable inbox for any new email. And if you require another temporary address the next day, the whole exercise has to be repeated.</p> \n<h2 id=\"disposable-email-addresses-with-gmail\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/disposable-email-address/28072/#disposable-email-addresses-with-gmail\" aria-label=\"disposable email addresses with gmail permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Disposable Email Addresses with Gmail</h2> \n<p>Here’s a new, simplified workflow that will let you use Gmail itself as a disposable email service provider.</p> \n<p>You’ll have just one temporary email address to remember and every time your share that email on the Internet, you attach an expiry date. Any email messages sent to your disposable Gmail account after the expiry date are discarded automatically else they are forwarded to your main account.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:526px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" class=\"language-text\">amit@gmail.com</code>. A website form requires your email address so you can put <code class=\"language-text\">amit+mmdd@gmail.com</code> in the sign-up field where <code class=\"language-text\">mmdd</code> is the month and date till when that disposable email will stay valid.</p> \n<p>For instance, if you specify the email address as <code class=\"language-text\">amit+0623@gmail.com</code> - that alias will be valid until June 23 and any emails sent to that alias after that date are ignored else they are forwarded to your main Gmail address. You can only specify the year in your temporary email <code class=\"language-text\">amit+12312020@gmail.com</code> in <code class=\"language-text\">mmddyyyy</code> format.</p> \n<h3 id=\"make-your-own-temporary-email-system-with-gmail\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/disposable-email-address/28072/#make-your-own-temporary-email-system-with-gmail\" aria-label=\"make your own temporary email system with gmail permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Make your own Temporary Email System with Gmail</h3> \n<p>Follow these steps to set up your own disposable email system in 2 minutes. Internally, it uses the <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/email/gmail-email-alias-two-separate-gmail-address/2388/\">Gmail plus trick</a> and some Google Apps Script magic.</p> \n<ol> \n <li><p>Create a new Gmail address (<a href=\"https://accounts.google.com/signup/v2/webcreateaccount?hl=en&amp;flowName=GlifWebSignIn&amp;flowEntry=SignUp\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">link</a>).</p></li> \n <li><p>While you are logged into your new Gmail account, <a href=\"https://script.google.com/d/1p1mElMVlqT0II8foeZI-zLAtbWz8JhrQGixTmXYXDHdeGAteTTOrBIdw/edit?newcopy=true\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">click here</a> to make a copy of the Google Script in your account.</p></li> \n <li><p>Inside the Google Script, go to line #13 and replace my email with the email address where you would like the temporary emails to be forwarded.</p></li> \n <li><p>Next, go to the Run menu, choose Run Function and select Initialize. Authorize the Google script and your disposable email system is up and running.</p></li> \n</ol> \n<p>The script will check your Gmail inbox every five minutes and process messages based on the expiry date in the message To field. You just have to set it once and forget about it.</p> \n<p>Your disposable address will last forever and yet it will protect your main inbox from spam. That’s it!</p> \n<h4 id=\"under-the-hood---how-it-works\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/disposable-email-address/28072/#under-the-hood---how-it-works\" aria-label=\"under the hood   how it works permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Under the Hood - How it works?</h4> \n<p>The Google Script is monitoring the temporary inbox using the Gmail API. If it discovers a new email that has an expiry date in the future, it simply forwards it to your main email account else it archives the message.</p> \n<p>Here’s the <a 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Auto Start the Embedded Slideshow</h3> \n<p>Append <code class=\"language-text\">start=true</code> to the URL and the slideshow will auto-play as soon as someone opens your webpage. Or set <code class=\"language-text\">start=false</code> and the slideshow will only play when the visitor click the play icon in the slides player.</p> \n<h3 id=\"change-the-duration-of-slides\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/embed-google-slides-200615#change-the-duration-of-slides\" aria-label=\"change the duration of slides permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Change the duration of slides</h3> \n<p>With <code class=\"language-text\">start</code> set to true, you can add <code class=\"language-text\">delayms=1000</code> to the URL to specify the time (in milliseconds) for which each slide should display before auto-advancing to the next one. For instance, <code class=\"language-text\">start=true&amp;delayms=6000</code>, the slideshow will autoplay and the slides will auto-advance every 6 seconds (6000 ms).</p> \n<h3 id=\"play-the-slideshow-in-loop\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/embed-google-slides-200615#play-the-slideshow-in-loop\" aria-label=\"play the slideshow in loop permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Play the slideshow in Loop</h3> \n<p>Add <code class=\"language-text\">restart=true</code> to the slideshow URL and it will play in a loop, meaning it will auto-advance to the first slide after the last one.</p> \n<h3 id=\"start-from-a-specific-slide\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/embed-google-slides-200615#start-from-a-specific-slide\" aria-label=\"start from a specific slide permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Start from a Specific Slide</h3> \n<p>Your embedded Google Slides presentation will always start from the first slide in the deck. You can however customize the URL to start the slideshow from a specific slide by adding <code class=\"language-text\">slide=id.p#</code> to the URL, where # is the slide number.</p> \n<p>For instance, if you wish to embed a slideshow with 8 seconds gap and starting from the 4th slide, your URL would be:</p> \n<p><code class=\"language-text\">https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/e/xxxx/embed?start=true&amp;delayms=8000&amp;slide=id.p4</code></p> \n<h3 id=\"remove-the-google-branding-and-player-control\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/embed-google-slides-200615#remove-the-google-branding-and-player-control\" aria-label=\"remove the google branding and player control permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Remove the Google Branding and Player Control</h3> \n<p>The Google Slides player displays the controls and Google branding in the bottom bar. However, if you wish to play the slideshow in kiosk mode without any player controls or Google Branding, just adding <code class=\"language-text\">rm=minimal</code> to the IFRAME link (rm = Render Mode)</p> \n<h3 id=\"make-the-google-slides-player-responsive\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/embed-google-slides-200615#make-the-google-slides-player-responsive\" aria-label=\"make the google slides player responsive permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Make the Google Slides player Responsive</h3> \n<p>The embed code provided by Google Slides has a fixed height and width and will thus display at the same size on both desktops and mobile screens. You can however make the player responsive with a little bit of CSS as detailed below.</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Remove the height, width and other parameters from the IFRAME tag:</li> \n</ol> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"html\"> \n <pre class=\"language-html\"><code class=\"language-html\"><span class=\"token tag\"><span class=\"token tag\"><span class=\"token punctuation\">&lt;</span>iframe</span> <span class=\"token attr-name\">src</span><span class=\"token attr-value\"><span class=\"token punctuation attr-equals\">=</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">\"</span>https://docs.google.com/presentation/d/e/xxxx/embed<span class=\"token punctuation\">\"</span></span><span class=\"token punctuation\">&gt;</span></span><span class=\"token tag\"><span class=\"token tag\"><span class=\"token punctuation\">&lt;/</span>iframe</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">&gt;</span></span>`</code></pre> \n</div> \n<ol start=\"2\"> \n <li>Add this CSS to your HTML page. The <code class=\"language-text\">padding-bottom</code> is set to 56.25% for 16x9 ratio (9/16*100) so the height of the player would be 56.25% of the player’s width. Set the value to 75% for a 4:3 ratio.</li> \n</ol> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"html\"> \n <pre class=\"language-html\"><code class=\"language-html\"><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span> <span class=\"token comment\">/* 16:9 Ratio */</span>\n    <span class=\"token property\">height</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> 0<span class=\"token 100% <span class=\"token important\">!important</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n    <span class=\"token property\">height</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">:</span> 100% <span output using the HTML service. When your publish your Google Script project as a web app, the script gets a public URL (think API) that can be invoked from external applications using either HTTP GET or POST requests with query parameters and request body.</p> \n<p>When publishing the script as a web app, make sure to choose “Allow anonymous access” and execute the script as yourself. If you edit the script, create a new version inside the script editor and deploy the latest version.</p> \n<p>Here are some examples that demonstrate how you can convert your Google Script into a web API by adding the <code class=\"language-text\">doGet</code> and <code class=\"language-text\">doPost</code> methods to your project.</p> \n<h3 id=\"handling-get-requests\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/code/19871-get-post-requests-google-script#handling-get-requests\" aria-label=\"handling get requests permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Handling GET Requests</h3> \n<p>When a script is published as a web app, the <code class=\"language-text\">doGet</code> callback function handles all GET requests made to the script’s public URL. requests in Google Script with utilities like CURL or Postman, ensure that that “Automatically follow redirects Follow HTTP 3xx responses as redirects” setting is turned on since the ContentService serves a 301 redirect from the <code class=\"language-text\">script.googleusercontent.com</code> domain.</p> \n<h4 id=\"serving-html-content\" style=\"position:relative\"><a focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Serving HTML Content</h4> \n<p>Your Google Apps script project can serve HTML web pages with the <code class=\"language-text\">HtmlService</code> service. The web pages served with App Script included Google warning header at the top but it can be removed if you embed the Google Script in another web page (like Google Sites) with the IFRAME tag.</p> class=\"language-text\">X-Frame-Options</code> header of the webpage to <code class=\"language-text\">XFrameOptionsMode.ALLOWALL</code> to allow other pages to embed your Google Script HTML page.</p> \n<h3 id=\"handle-post-requests-with-google-scripts\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/code/19871-get-post-requests-google-script#handle-post-requests-with-google-scripts\" aria-label=\"handle post requests with google scripts permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" \n  </svg></a>Handle POST Requests with Google Scripts</h3> \n<p>The callback function <code class=\"language-text\">doPost</code> is invoked when an HTTP POST request is make to your Google Script URL that is published as a web app with anonymous access.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\"><span class=\"token keyword\">const</span> <span class=\"token function-variable function\">doPost</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token parameter\">request</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span> <span class=\"token operator\">=&gt;</span> <span class=\"token punctuation\">{</span>\n  console<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">log</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>request<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n  <span class=\"token keyword\">return</span> ContentService<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">crateTextOutput</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token constant\">JSON</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token function\">stringify</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>request<span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span>\n<span class=\"token punctuation\">}</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">;</span></code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>The <code class=\"language-text\">request</code> argument of the doPost method can include:</p> \n<ol> \n <li><p><code class=\"language-text\">queryString</code> - The name-value pairs sent in the URL of the request (name=Mike&amp;age=12)</p></li> \n <li><p><code class=\"language-text\">parameter</code> - The query string name-value pairs are also accessible inside the parameter object similar to GET requests (e.paremeter.name or e.parameter.age).</p></li> \n <li><p><code class=\"language-text\">postData</code> - The contents property of the postData object includes the POST body and type property of postData specifies the MIME type of the post body. It can have values like <code class=\"language-text\">application/x-www-form-urlencoded</code> (key-value pairs separated by the ’&amp;’ character and each key is separated from its encoded value by ’=’), <code class=\"language-text\">application/json</code> for JSON data or <code class=\"language-text\">text/plain</code> for text body.</p></li> \n</ol> \n<p>For binary data, like <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/file-upload-google-forms/29170/\">file uploads</a>, the HTTP post request is sent with the <code class=\"language-text\">multipart/form-data</code> mime type. In the case of <code class=\"language-text\">application/x-www-form-urlencoded</code>, the queryString is set as part of the POST request body.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" Apps Script service. even search engines that find your sheet that has the Charts data.</p> \n<p>We are using this <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1YpiTo7Fc3QvBdbuReCIcwtg7lnmZupQAH57phrDLotI/edit#gid=0\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 \n<p>Here specify the URL of your publish Google Spreadsheet (the gid should point to the sheet that has the data). The Google Visualization API Query Language (<a href=\"https://developers.google.com/chart/interactive/docs/querylanguage\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">reference</a>) lets you use SQL like syntax to specify columns that should be used for fetching data from the Google sheet. You can also use <code class=\"language-text\">offset</code>, <code class=\"language-text\">where</code> and <code class=\"language-text\">limit</code> clauses to limit the data that is returned by Google Sheets.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\">google<span class=\"token 00:45:54","updatedTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","title":"Google Maps Formulas for Google Sheets","link":"https://www.labnol.org/google-maps-sheets-200817","description":"<p>You can bring the power of Google Maps to your Google Sheets using simple formulas with no coding. You don’t need to sign-up for the Google Maps API and all results from Google Maps are cached in the sheet so you are unlikely to hit any quota limits.</p> \n<p>To give you a quick example, if you have the starting address in column A and the destination address in column B, a formula like <code class=\"language-text\">=GOOGLEMAPS_DISTANCE(A1, B1, \"driving\")</code> will quickly calculate the distance between the two points.</p> \n<p>Or modify the formula slightly <code class=\"language-text\">=GOOGLEMAPS_TIME(A1, B1, \"walking\")</code> to know how long it will take for a person to walk from one point to another.</p> \n<p>If you would like to try the Google Maps formulas without getting into the technical details, just make a copy of this <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1_WsL9KIhUYz5_6imBnjticTfa4g004YAfLrlK4Ix6w8/copy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Google Sheet</a> and you are all set.</p> tutorial explains how you can easily write custom Google Maps functions inside Google Sheets that will help you:</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Calculate distances between two cities or any addresses.</li> \n <li>Calculate the travel time (walking, driving or biking) between two points.</li> \n <li>Get the latitude and longitude co-ordinates of any address on Google Maps.</li> \n <li>Use reverse geocoding to find the postal address from GPS co-ordinates.</li> \n <li>Print driving directions between any points on earth.</li> \n <li>Get the address from the zip code itself.</li> \n</ol> \n<h4 improve performance by caching results permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 </svg></a>Tip: Improve Performance by Caching Results</h4> \n<p>All the above Google Sheets functions internally use the Google Maps API to calculate routes, distances and travel time. Google offers a limited quota for Maps operations and if your sheet performs too many queries in a short duration, you are likely to see errors like \"\"Service invoked too many times for one day” or something similar.</p> \n<p>To get around this problem, it is recommended that you use Apps Script’s built-in cache to store results and, if the results of a function already exist in the case, you’ll make one less request to Google Maps The Maps functions inside this <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1_WsL9KIhUYz5_6imBnjticTfa4g004YAfLrlK4Ix6w8/copy\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Google Sheet</a> also use caching and here’s how you can implement it.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre For instance, if you have a sheet containing orders from different countries, you can set up a country filter to hide all rows where the country is not the United States.</p> \n<p>If you have a Google Script that iterates through each row in the Google Sheet for performing actions on the row, like <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/mail_merge_with_attachments/223404411203\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">sending emails</a>&nbsp;or <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/document_studio/429444628321\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">merging documents</a>, you can check for the hidden and filtered rows and easily skip them from the workflow.</p> \n<p>There are two ways to check for hidden and filtered rows in Google Sheets. You can either use the SpreadsheetApp service of Google Scripts or use the Spreadsheet V4 API.</p> \n<h3 id=\"check-for-hidden-rows-with-google-scripts\" style=\"position:relative\"><a id=\"spreadsheets-quota-limitation\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/code/20611-get-hidden-and-filtered-rows-in-google-sheets#spreadsheets-quota-limitation\" aria-label=\"spreadsheets quota limitation permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Spreadsheets Quota Limitation</h3> \n<p>Google Spreadsheets Quota will allow your addon project to make up 100 Spreadsheet reads per 100 seconds and this limit is shared across all users of the project. Thus if your project has too many simultaneous users, the Spreadsheet service may fail with the error:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">API call to sheets.spreadsheets.get failed with error: Quota exceeded for quota group 'ReadGroup' and limit 'Read requests per 100 seconds' of service 'sheets.googleapis.com'</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>To stay withing the quota, you can either cache the results of the expensive <code class=\"language-text\">getHiddenRows</code> method or use a try-catch block. If the Spreadsheet API fails due to quota error, use the SpreadsheetApp service to check for hidden rows.</p> \n<p>Also, a row in the Google Sheet can be filtered and hidden at the same time.</p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 15 May 2020 13:37:33 +0000","feedId":259,"bgimg":"https://www.labnol.org/static/5bab52935dfbe23b196a5553fef1e580/16546/google-sheet-hide-filter.png","linkMd5":"dd586f12af903478c0c0d92599e16371","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn83@2020_1/2020/08/17/16-46-08-903_773c4f154bd45348.webp","destWidth":720,"destHeight":612,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.labnol.org/static/5bab52935dfbe23b196a5553fef1e580/16546/google-sheet-hide-filter.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx3/cdn83@2020_1/2020/08/17/16-46-08-903_773c4f154bd45348.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","updatedTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","title":"How to Track Unsubscribes with Mail Merge for Gmail","link":"https://www.labnol.org/track-unsubscribes-gmail-7047","description":"<p>Mail Merge for Gmail gives you can easy option to add an “Unsubscribe” link to all your outgoing email campaigns. unsubscribe option is checked, all outgoing emails sent through Gmail Mail merge will include a remove link in the message footer automatically.&nbsp; The subscriber can click the link to opt-out of&nbsp;your future mailing lists.</p> \n<p>When they click the unsubscribe link, they are taken to a special landing page confirming that their request for unsubscribing has been successfully recorded.</p> \n<h3 id=\"how-to-view-unsubscribed-user-reports\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/track-unsubscribes-gmail-7047#how-to-view-unsubscribed-user-reports\" \n  </svg></a>How to View Unsubscribed User Reports</h3> \n<p>Go to Add-ons &gt; Mail Merge with Attachments &gt; Campaign Reports &gt; Open and Click Reports. This will open a list of email campaigns you’ve sent through Mail Merge. Click the Unsubscribe button in any specific campaign to generate a list of all email addresses that have unsubscribed from your mailing list via that particular campaign.</p> \n<p>This will add a new “Unsubscribe Report” sheet in your Google Spreadsheet for Mail Merge. The report will include the following data to help you analyze the campaigns that resulted in the most unsubscribes:</p> \n<ul> \n <li>Date when the message was sent to the user</li> \n <li>Date when the user unsubscribed from the mailing list</li> \n <li>Email address of the unsubscriber</li> \n <li>Location / IP address from where the user unsubscribed</li> \n <li>Web browser (or mobile browser) of the unsubscriber.</li> \n</ul> \n<p>Here’s a sample unsubscribe report generated by Mail merge.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" \n<p>Google Slides has a built-in option for exporting your slides as a PDF file and this can be configured to also include the speaker notes.</p> \n<p>Open your deck in Google Slides, go to the File menu and choose Print Settings and Preview. Here choose the “1 slide with note” option and click the “Download PDF” button to export your speaker notes as PDF.</p> \n<p>It just works but the only downside with this approach is that it generates a bloated PDF that isn’t perfect for printing. Also, the slides are always includd with the speakers notes in the PDF, there’s currently no option to save the speaker notes only.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" create a <a href=\"https://marketplace.zoom.us/develop/create\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">new app</a>. Choose <code class=\"language-text\">JWT</code> as the app type and make a note of the Zoom API key and secret. We can build Zoom apps with the OAuth2 library as well but since this app is only for internal use and will not be publish to the Zoom marketplace, the JWT approach is easier.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/23056/130818.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:69.44444444444444%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Create Zoom App\" title=\"Create Zoom App\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/16546/130818.png\" srcSet=\"/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/96042/130818.png 180w,/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/7a322/130818.png 360w,/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/16546/130818.png 720w,/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/6d80e/130818.png 1080w,/static/9624823fa79c62dc87540710a9a6949c/23056/130818.png 1134w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>The app would involve two step. We’ll connect to the <code class=\"language-text\">/api.zoom.us/v2/users/</code> API to get the Zoom ID of current authenticated user. Next, we make a POST request to the <code class=\"language-text\">/v2/users/&lt;&lt;ZoomUserId&gt;&gt;/meetings</code> endpoint to create the actual Zoom meeting.</p> \n<h3 style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/submit-blogger-sitemap-to-google/10149/#the-problem-with-blogger-sitemap-files\" aria-label=\"the problem with blogger sitemap files permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>The Problem with Blogger Sitemap Files</h3> \n<p>A complete XML sitemap file should mention all pages of a site but that’s not the case if your blog is hosted on the Blogger or blogspot platform.</p> \n<p>Google accepts sitemaps in XML, RSS, or Atom formats. They <a href=\"https://webmasters.googleblog.com/2014/10/best-practices-for-xml-sitemaps-rssatom.html\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">recommend</a> use both XML sitemaps and RSS/Atom feeds for optimal crawling.</p> \n<p>The default atom RSS feed of any Blogger blog will have only the most recent blog posts – <a href=\"http://googleblog.blogspot.com/atom.xml?redirect=false\" title=\"XML Sitemap for Google Blog\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">see example</a>. That’s a limitation because some of your older blog pages, that are missing in the default XML sitemap file, may never get indexed in search engines. There’s however a simple solution to fix this problem.</p> \n<h3 id=\"generate-xml-sitemap-for-your-blogger-blog\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/submit-blogger-sitemap-to-google/10149/#generate-xml-sitemap-for-your-blogger-blog\" aria-label=\"generate xml sitemap for your blogger blog permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Generate XML Sitemap for your Blogger Blog</h3> \n<p>This section is valid for both regular Blogger blogs (that have a <code class=\"language-text\">blogspot.com</code> address) and also the self-hosted Blogger blogs that use a custom domain (like postsecret.com).</p> \n<p>Here’s what you need to do to expose your blog’s complete site structure to search engines with the help of an XML sitemap.</p> \n<ol> \n <li><p>Open the <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/blogger/sitemap\"><strong>Sitemap Generator</strong></a> and type the full address of your Blogger blog.</p></li> \n <li><p>Click the Generate Sitemap button and this tool will instantly create the XML file with your sitemap. Copy the entire text to your clipboard.</p></li> \n <li><p>Next, go to your Blogger.com dashboard, navigate to Settings –&gt; Search Preferences, enable Custom robots.txt option (available in the Crawling and Indexing section). Paste the XML sitemap here and save your changes.</p></li> \n</ol> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/b67d5d2f88ad39e2092581e97d926f60/2e506/140340.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:70%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;background-image:url('data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAABQAAAAOCAYAAAAvxDzwAAAACXBIWXMAAAsSAAALEgHS3X78AAACCUlEQVQ4y4VTa2/aQBD0//9D/VSRCiKC1Kpqo5CmxdjBxg8Ov+5s8Hu6uwkpTZBYaTjfcTc3O7tnhc4j0niNaLtFQEj2e/r24Twt8bx6EnjrP/DP4Nk0OjYiz4X/7MIj+O5a5lYVB1BxjCAI4TgObNvGiuD7W4RhSIiQJAnSNKUxlXFPo0oyFFpjnxmo3CBUCb7/fIBlQh8b10VRFChLIwfSNEFd1xjHEX3fo+u6i2jbFh2ja9E0DXwSZUWFhspytLRwimEYZDNvYkImHmltOIOsneEUVk7KWDoH/8HKsiwTmLKUNSZvT8RXYFVVCaWUEHHwuNvtYIzB6V65oKxkfpWQCdi3gRRwcJpMJiDl/5L5GBcJTXWQqp3ieDyKYi7SwJucFSoibqkIfHlNFx7qDj3NL/lodSZHrTOMj/csD/0wCilXkaN3bWzsFdbUUhV52nU9jk0vRXoffMYaKwOtYujfv9AeDh9S4th4HlwiFOV5Turz175MxF/+Zou4+hYfifcJKrq5Yx8vpPGwXGI+n2M6nWI2m2F+d4cvNzeYTCYyZywWC+kGq/vxDTrwUCYKJfn2n0L+0QUi34NDzb+lpxlFEWJ5WYGAXxOvMV4IdxEKtaN0q7c0pXm579iX5T2a209ovn6m4hTAlapbRzJSk9mFNm+V1FTVnLxqXl9PlaWEREy/9ErO7fkL6Y8zzL66IssAAAAASUVORK5CYII=');background-size:cover;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Blogger XML Sitemap\" title=\"Blogger XML Sitemap\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/b67d5d2f88ad39e2092581e97d926f60/16546/140340.png\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>And we are done. Search engines will automatically discover your XML sitemap files via the robots.txt file and you don’t have to ping them manually.</p> \n<p>Internally, the XML sitemap generator counts all the blog posts that are available in your Blogger blog. It then splits the posts in batches of 500 posts each and generates multiple XML feed for each batch. Thus search engines will be able to discover every single post on your blog since it would be part of one of these XML sitemaps.</p> \n<p>PS: If you have switched from Blogger to WordPress, it still makes sense to submit XML sitemaps of your old Blogspot blog as that will aid search engines discover your new WordPress blog posts and pages.</p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Thu, 14 May 2020 15:05:57 +0000","feedId":259,"bgimg":"https://www.labnol.org/static/eaa88e069fdc132899cb45bb36e2b6ac/b30f8/xml-sitemap.png","linkMd5":"59309a5a48bd3b4b8477e767f4e6ebf9","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn25@2020_3/2020/08/17/16-46-08-956_b49ff6b14a1c2deb.webp","destWidth":500,"destHeight":200,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.labnol.org/static/eaa88e069fdc132899cb45bb36e2b6ac/b30f8/xml-sitemap.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn25@2020_3/2020/08/17/16-46-08-956_b49ff6b14a1c2deb.webp","https://www.labnol.org/static/b67d5d2f88ad39e2092581e97d926f60/16546/140340.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx4/cdn40@2020_3/2020/08/17/16-46-11-748_85b11f63a13b9de1.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","updatedTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","title":"How to Use Conditional Fields in Email Templates","link":"https://www.labnol.org/conditional-email-merge-fields-200626","description":"<p>The <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/mail_merge_with_attachments/223404411203\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Mail Merge</a> and <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/document_studio/429444628321\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Document Studio</a> add-ons let you send personalized emails with the help of template markers.</p> \n<p>The markers automatically create a mapping between the column names in the Google Sheet and the variable fields in your email message. When the email is sent, the marker fields in the email message are replaced with the values from the respective columns of the sheet.</p> \n<p>Let’s say you have a column titled <code class=\"language-text\">First Name</code> in your Google Sheet and your email message body has a marker that says <code class=\"language-text\">Dear {{First Name}},</code> (also notice the comma in the end).</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:676px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/defdd716768425dd4f0fe1159c2a6729/080e7/182420.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:78.88888888888889%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;background-image:url('data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAABQAAAAQCAYAAAAWGF8bAAAACXBIWXMAAAsSAAALEgHS3X78AAACh0lEQVQ4y5WUS2sUQRSF+4f6B5JAsou/QPdqlAyDARfGrQvFCD5wIS7ETcgQFWfS8+5ndderH9U9fbxVk4jGJGjDx60aqDun7jnd3nEywqfFKbIoxXA4dBRFAa01hJToOvzX4w3SMT4H3yBZjmWwxGKxQMYY4jiGEAJPDw+xvbOD3d3b2NrawsbGJjY2r8ezXbumQ8YVEsZRmxW4UDBt53j77j329h7i8cEB+v0+9vf30ev1rsVjWY44nIMtfcTzIV19ChaMCdrPhlAiR10bVFX1b1eWusJk8BEnR48wePUAp2/6OHndc+vjl/cx+foFYZxgPPaRpinatoUxBk3TXIlXlBWCIEBI87NPxlJM6HBdlTB15eaolHLVHrj8dOTaBU6hLirMJj6mZ99RazJmOsLZj1NEizFKyZAmMWazGXzfd4xGI1I7djVJEmceIxOjKHJ719AeWs7HKBSH5AzhcgqeJai0gOC5U2iRFCOr9KLa619W6UUJg5IcndEwpXS0tXJowaCVvNGE7lJQqWEGSU42583qQjjsupAZ/Zn4S8VNeEoXKAuFpqLsWcp1bWpNDe115ZVKro2NUHRQkaKCQm0hY2w1paArp6Seo111aNoVqvM8rlarX9H5PUJ2ph6Xit5dmpkpSFVB6rSrrSlRaumC3VLzrpbI4gXm87kzKMsycM6R5/kfe09IDU2mGJ05dZWyNSOHaa4qwcBn2H4mcKvPcPcFp2jE648HYd22TWxkOKfZ17VtqGiGGm1ToTFEXa4rsSLVfiBw7yjGnechnnyI6QUInCobG4tVZvN38ZtnPwQ2HrWk3MkUpbB1TSFiGBkBhmiIKkLBY6gsJAJXJQug89Bh1z8Bg36rMmonxO8AAAAASUVORK5CYII=');background-size:cover;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Template Fields in Mail Merge\" title=\"Template Fields in Mail Merge\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/defdd716768425dd4f0fe1159c2a6729/080e7/182420.png\" srcSet=\"/static/defdd716768425dd4f0fe1159c2a6729/96042/182420.png style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<h3 id=\"fill-in-fields\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/conditional-email-merge-fields-200626#fill-in-fields\" aria-label=\"fill in fields permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Fill-in Fields</h3> \n<p>If your Google Sheet rows has a value, say Alex, the text in the email message would read <code class=\"language-text\">Dear Alex,</code>. However, if the first name is not available for a particular row, the variable field would be replaced with a blank value and this first line in the email message would thus read <code class=\"language-text\">Dear &lt;space&gt;,</code> - something that you should totally avoid in personalized emails.</p> \n<p>There are two ways to deal with this issue. You can either clean up your data before running merge, or you can use formulas in Google Sheets to offer an alternate value in case the original field doesn’t have a value. Let me explain:</p> \n<ol> \n <li><p>Add a new column in the Google Sheet title “Greeting”</p></li> \n <li><p>Add a formula in row #2 of the Greeting column.</p></li> \n</ol> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">=IF(ISBLANK(A2),\"Hello\",CONCATENATE(\"Dear\", \" \", A2))</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>The formula basically looks at the Name column, it is blank, the greeting is set to “Hello” else it uses the default “Hello FirstName” value.</p> \n<ol start=\"3\"> \n <li>Now edit your email template and replace “Dear {{Name}},” with “{{Greeting}},“.</li> \n</ol> \n<p>You can either copy-paste the formula in the remaining cells of the column manually or use the <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/arrayformula-copy-formulas-in-entire-column/29711/\">ArrayFormula function</a> to copy it down for you.</p> \n<h3 id=\"ifthenelse\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/conditional-email-merge-fields-200626#ifthenelse\" aria-label=\"ifthenelse permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>If..Then..Else</h3> \n<p>The technique can be extended to add more customization to your email message. For instance, you may choose a different greeting in your email subject based on the country of the recipient.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/89c55/184745.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:34.44444444444444%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;background-image:url('data:image/png;base64,iVBORw0KGgoAAAANSUhEUgAAABQAAAAHCAYAAAAIy204AAAACXBIWXMAAAsSAAALEgHS3X78AAABVElEQVQoz3WRy07CQBSG+/6v4QVdmLh0qUBMjAt3pJQCTemFsZ37tJSW8jsdQI2JTb58c86ZOXOp55MIJM2wWq+gtYYQAnVdo+s6R9u2jt/xxX3f4/QdzzrCyyQFLTko49Cmsk0rSKWhtIGyHnKmqlHVO8dQk1KB2flD3HYH2/iI7tAP/eBJWqAgGYxkqBRzZgXBNt2A5Cl2RqLWApXmrqYtvCQOVmxRbDNIXoBTAiUovMX7E4KXawTTeyzfHhFMRpiN77B4fYD/fIX5+AbBHxaT22/C6cjmfmKP5An2tbQ7fEKwAl1ToaQcbbNDv9c4NAaHvaXRNj7Z5Zz1uWZcrbP24mhpj1qC5iuQaIZKFvjwUwTLDVZpgnmaIs4yhEmCwP68KMuxtuPQ2t/ECNMcszjCPE5QGwVveLfGCOwNdew0gxQMSgr7+CfUP76MOSvtGu5u+gUjBAskmnpMAAAAAABJRU5ErkJggg==');background-size:cover;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Email Greetings\" title=\"Email Greetings\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/16546/184745.png\" srcSet=\"/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/96042/184745.png 180w,/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/7a322/184745.png 360w,/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/16546/184745.png 720w,/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/89c55/184745.png 854w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>If the country is in column B, the Greeting formula would be:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">=IFNA(\n  IFS(\n   B2 = \"USA\", \"Hello\",\n   B2 = \"Spain\", \"Hola\",\n   B2 = \"India\", \"Namaste\"\n  ), \"Greetings\")</code></pre> \n</div> \n<h3 id=\"calculated-fields\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/conditional-email-merge-fields-200626#calculated-fields\" aria-label=\"calculated fields permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Calculated Fields</h3> \n<p>The templates fields in the email message are dumb and merely get replaced by values in the Google Sheet. If you wish to include any logic or calculations in the template fields, it should be done in the sheet itself.</p> \n<p>Let me give you another example.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/b6e86/194500.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:76.66666666666666%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Conditional Fields in Mail Merge\" title=\"Conditional Fields in Mail Merge\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/16546/194500.png\" srcSet=\"/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/96042/194500.png 180w,/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/7a322/194500.png 360w,/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/16546/194500.png 720w,/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/b6e86/194500.png 851w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>The Google Sheet records the invoice details and <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/send-reminder-emails-200425\">sends email reminders</a> for payments. Using the magic of Google Sheet formulas and template markers, the text of the email message can be dynamically changed based on when the invoice is due. If the due date has already passed, we send a different message.</p> \n<p>First add a new column (say, Days Left) that calculates the number days between now and the invoice due date. Add this formula in row #2 of the column. It will only fill values when the due date is available.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">=ArrayFormula(IF(ISBLANK(C2:C),\"\", ROUND(C2:C-TODAY())))</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>Add a new “Invoice Status” column and again use the <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/internet/arrayformula-copy-formulas-in-entire-column/29711/\">ArrayFormula function</a> to get the text for the email message body and subject.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"text\"> \n <pre class=\"language-text\"><code class=\"language-text\">=ArrayFormula(\n  IF(ISBLANK(C2:C), \"\" ,\n     IF(D2:D&gt;0, CONCAT(\"due on \",TEXT(C2:C,\"mmmm dd, yyyy\")),\n                CONCAT(ABS(D2:D),\" days past due\"))))</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>See more <a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/topic/google-sheets/\">Google Sheets solutions</a>.</p>","descriptionType":"html","publishedDate":"Fri, 26 Jun 2020 00:00:00 +0000","feedId":259,"bgimg":"https://www.labnol.org/static/defdd716768425dd4f0fe1159c2a6729/080e7/182420.png","linkMd5":"ff2c97082ced04211282bef8ede327d2","bgimgJsdelivr":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn81@2020_1/2020/08/17/16-46-08-859_f2ab558cfc770fe7.webp","destWidth":676,"destHeight":532,"author":"","articleImgCdnMap":{"https://www.labnol.org/static/defdd716768425dd4f0fe1159c2a6729/080e7/182420.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx16/cdn81@2020_1/2020/08/17/16-46-08-859_f2ab558cfc770fe7.webp","https://www.labnol.org/static/f733b4321cb80c0e463a66020bb9639f/16546/184745.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx23/cdn95@2020_2/2020/08/17/16-46-11-288_16f147b671bf35ca.webp","https://www.labnol.org/static/c98ee517ec5f023d370aed1342d008eb/16546/194500.png":"https://cdn.jsdelivr.net/gh/myreaderx10/cdn72@2020_4/2020/08/17/16-46-11-556_4615931d2bb0f124.webp"}},{"createdTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","updatedTime":"2020-08-18 00:45:54","title":"How to Send Google Forms with Pre-filled Answers","link":"https://www.labnol.org/prefilled-google-forms-200601","description":"<p><a href=\"https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=vcEju__MPtw\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Prefilled Google Forms</a>, where some of the fields in the form are pre-populated with answers you already have, make the process of filling out your forms easier and faster.</p> \n<ol> \n <li>Your contacts are more likely to fill out the form as it takes less time for them to complete the remaining fields.</li> \n <li>The form respondents are less likely to type incorrect data in fields, like the employee ID, that are pre-populated.</li> \n <li>The forms feels more personal when people see their name and other personalized information pre-filled in the form.</li> \n</ol> \n<h3 id=\"create-pre-filled-google-forms-with-google-sheets\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/prefilled-google-forms-200601#create-pre-filled-google-forms-with-google-sheets\" aria-label=\"create pre filled google forms with google sheets permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Create Pre-filled Google Forms with Google Sheets</h3> \n<p>This step-by-step video tutorial explains how you can create pre-filled Google Forms with dynamic information from a Google Sheet. You can then use <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/mail_merge_with_attachments/223404411203\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Mail Merge</a> or <a href=\"https://gsuite.google.com/marketplace/app/document_studio/429444628321\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Document Studio</a> to automatically send the prefilled forms to your contacts in bulk with Gmail.</p> \n<p><iframe width=\"100%\" height=\"315\" src=\"https://www.youtube-nocookie.com/embed/vcEju__MPtw?rel=0\" frameBorder=\"0\" allow=\"accelerometer; autoplay; encrypted-media; gyroscope; picture-in-picture\" allowfullscreen=\"\"></iframe></p> \n<p>In our example, the organization maintains their employee database in a Google Spreadsheet and they want to give employees an option to self-update their details in the spreadsheet with the help of Google Forms.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/2ed7f/120356.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:40.55555555555556%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Google Spreadsheet with Answers\" title=\"Google Spreadsheet with Answers\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/16546/120356.png\" srcSet=\"/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/96042/120356.png 180w,/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/7a322/120356.png 360w,/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/16546/120356.png 720w,/static/03bbbc1c6f01ee6f574bec4f9c92a083/2ed7f/120356.png 867w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>If you look at employee records in the Google Sheet carefully, you’ll find that only some details of the employees are missing in the sheet. This is a perfect use case for using prefilled Google Forms as it be wasting employee productivity if we send them a blank Google Form and require them to fill out every single field.</p> \n<p>For instance, in row #2, we know the location and gender of Angus but his date of birth is unavailable in our records. For row #4, the employee ID and email is known but Kiran’s other details are missing.</p> \n<h4 id=\"create-the-google-form\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/prefilled-google-forms-200601#create-the-google-form\" aria-label=\"create the google form permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Create the Google Form</h4> \n<p>To build this workflow, we’ll create a Google Form with fields corresponding to the columns in the source Google Sheet. Here’s how the final form would look like:</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/81bb733264ea2585ce88022fe00944a1/7b99c/123826.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:70%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"123826\" title=\"123826\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/81bb733264ea2585ce88022fe00944a1/16546/123826.png\" srcSet=\"/static/81bb733264ea2585ce88022fe00944a1/96042/123826.png sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<h4 fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Generate the Prefilled Form Link</h4> \n<p>Inside the Google Form editor, click the 3-dot menu choose the <code class=\"language-text\">Get pre-filled link</code> option. Here, fill in every field with dummy data that is easy to recognize and replace later. Once the fields have been filled, click the <code class=\"language-text\">Get Link</code> button to generate the prefilled link and copy it to your clipboard.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/0d847be72cedd96da1d7e5bd4b84f293/d251d/125328.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"Prefilled Google Form\" title=\"Prefilled Google Form\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/0d847be72cedd96da1d7e5bd4b84f293/16546/125328.png\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<p>The link to the prefilled Google Form would look something like this.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\">https<span class=\"token operator\">:</span><span class=\"token operator\">/</span><span class=\"token operator\">/</span>docs<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>google<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span>com<span class=\"token operator\">/</span>forms<span class=\"token operator\">/</span>d<span class=\"token operator\">/</span>e<span class=\"token operator\">/</span>xxxx<span class=\"token operator\">/</span>viewform\n   <span class=\"token operator\">?</span>entry<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token number\">1808207196</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token constant\">EMPLOYEEID</span><span class=\"token operator\">&amp;</span>entry<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token number\">1663131167</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token constant\">EMPLOYEENAME</span>\n   <span class=\"token operator\">&amp;</span>entry<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token number\">1819275928</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token number\">2020</span><span class=\"token operator\">-</span><span class=\"token number\">06</span><span class=\"token operator\">-</span><span class=\"token number\">03</span><span class=\"token operator\">&amp;</span>entry<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token number\">2071782719</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span>Female\n   <span class=\"token operator\">&amp;</span>entry<span class=\"token punctuation\">.</span><span class=\"token number\">175059757</span><span class=\"token operator\">=</span>Hyderabad</code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>It’s long and complex but if you take a closer look, this is simply a collection of name and value pairs appended to the Google Form URL. Google Forms will assign a unique id to each field in the form and these are appended to the Form URL with your pre-populated value.</p> \n<p>For instance, the Name field in your Google Form is internally represented as <code class=\"language-text\">entry.1663131167</code> in the form URL. If we replace the parameter value <code class=\"language-text\">EMPLOYEENAME</code> in the URL with another value, that would be prepopulated in the Google Form.</p> \n<p>And this is exactly what we’ll do to create personalized prefilled links for all the rows in our Google Sheet.</p> \n<p><span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-wrapper\" style=\"position:relative;display:block;margin-left:auto;margin-right:auto;max-width:720px\"> <a class=\"gatsby-resp-image-link\" href=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/8ba7d/prefilled-google-forms.png\" style=\"display:block\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"noopener\"> <span class=\"gatsby-resp-image-background-image\" style=\"padding-bottom:62.22222222222222%;position:relative;bottom:0;left:0;display:block\"></span> <img class=\"gatsby-resp-image-image\" alt=\"prefilled google forms\" title=\"prefilled google forms\" src=\"https://www.labnol.org/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/16546/prefilled-google-forms.png\" srcSet=\"/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/96042/prefilled-google-forms.png 180w,/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/7a322/prefilled-google-forms.png 360w,/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/16546/prefilled-google-forms.png 720w,/static/db62a47f842086647ee7566dd3bf8450/8ba7d/prefilled-google-forms.png 1066w\" sizes=\"(max-width: 720px) 100vw, 720px\" style=\"width:100%;height:100%;margin:0;vertical-align:middle;position:absolute;top:0;left:0\" loading=\"lazy\" /> </a> </span></p> \n<h4 id=\"add-form-formulas-in-google-sheet\" style=\"position:relative\"><a href=\"https://www.labnol.org/prefilled-google-forms-200601#add-form-formulas-in-google-sheet\" aria-label=\"add form formulas in google sheet permalink\" class=\"anchor before\"> \n  <svg aria-hidden=\"true\" focusable=\"false\" height=\"16\" version=\"1.1\" viewBox=\"0 0 16 16\" width=\"16\"> \n   <path fill-rule=\"evenodd\" d=\"M4 9h1v1H4c-1.5 0-3-1.69-3-3.5S2.55 3 4 3h4c1.45 0 3 1.69 3 3.5 0 1.41-.91 2.72-2 3.25V8.59c.58-.45 1-1.27 1-2.09C10 5.22 8.98 4 8 4H4c-.98 0-2 1.22-2 2.5S3 9 4 9zm9-3h-1v1h1c1 0 2 1.22 2 2.5S13.98 12 13 12H9c-.98 0-2-1.22-2-2.5 0-.83.42-1.64 1-2.09V6.25c-1.09.53-2 1.84-2 3.25C6 11.31 7.55 13 9 13h4c1.45 0 3-1.69 3-3.5S14.5 6 13 6z\"></path> \n  </svg></a>Add Form Formulas in Google Sheet</h4> \n<p>Inside your Google Spreadsheet, create a new sheet and rename it Form Link. Paste the prefilled Google Form link in the first cell (A1) of this blank sheet.</p> \n<p>Next return to the Google Sheet that has the employee database and create a new column, say Google Form Link.</p> \n<p>Now we need to replace the dummy values in our prefilled link with the actual values from the rows in the sheet and this can be easily done with <code class=\"language-text\">SUBSTITUTE</code> function of Google Sheets.</p> \n<p>For instance, we need replace <code class=\"language-text\">EMPLOYEENAME</code> in the prefilled link with real names that are in column B of the spreadsheet. Our formula would be something like this:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\"> <span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token string\">'Form Link'</span><span class=\"token operator\">!</span>$<span class=\"token constant\">A</span>$<span class=\"token number\">1</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"EMPLOYEENAME\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">B2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span></code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>We’ll feed the result of this formula into another <code class=\"language-text\">SUBSTITUTE</code> function to replace another field, say EMPLOYEEID.</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\"><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n   <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token string\">'Form Link'</span><span class=\"token operator\">!</span>$<span class=\"token constant\">A</span>$<span class=\"token number\">1</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"EMPLOYEENAME\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">B2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n   <span class=\"token string\">\"EMPLOYEEID\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">A2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span></code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>This has to be repeated for every prefilled field in the Google Form.</p> \n<p>If your prefilled data contains space, you need to wrap the results into another SUBSTITUTE function that will replace all occurrences of spaces with the plus symbol.</p> \n<p>Our final prefilled link would be:</p> \n<div class=\"gatsby-highlight\" data-language=\"javascript\"> \n <pre class=\"language-javascript\"><code class=\"language-javascript\"><span class=\"token operator\">=</span><span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n  <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n   <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n    <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n     <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span>\n      <span class=\"token constant\">SUBSTITUTE</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">(</span><span class=\"token string\">'Form Link'</span><span class=\"token operator\">!</span>$<span class=\"token constant\">A</span>$<span class=\"token number\">1</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"EMPLOYEEID\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">A2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n     <span class=\"token string\">\"EMPLOYEENAME\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">B2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n    <span class=\"token string\">\"2020-05-31\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span><span class=\"token constant\">E2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n   <span class=\"token string\">\"Female\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">C2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n  <span class=\"token string\">\"Hyderabad\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token constant\">D2</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span>\n <span class=\"token string\">\" \"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">,</span> <span class=\"token string\">\"+\"</span><span class=\"token punctuation\">)</span></code></pre> \n</div> \n<p>You can test the workflow using this <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/forms/d/e/1FAIpQLSc1sQ6mCgcNkt9OFhhwVosVodBm-LRVAAub_iSjGG-pSpt2gQ/viewform?usp=pp_url&amp;entry.1808207196=A005&amp;entry.1663131167=Jacob+Friedman&amp;entry.1819275928=1930-07-29&amp;entry.2071782719=&amp;entry.175059757=\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">prefilled Google Form</a> that will write your form submission in a new row of this <a href=\"https://docs.google.com/spreadsheets/d/1YB_TS8e97z81BWp5UgSNhugfjZmI7ETJSTm3czR_wYU/edit#gid=1535453044\" target=\"_blank\" rel=\"nofollow noopener noreferrer\">Google Sheet</a>.</p> \n<h4 you plan to prefill dates in the Google Form, you need rewrite your dates in the Google Sheets in a format that Google Forms can recognize.</p> \n<p>This is easy to implement.
